{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01CsUkw7T1w62Zu4B5WWJHSq","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_018CRw8PT5KwTTmjGmZuCHCP","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and Apply Configurations: A Deep Technical Guide\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nKubernetes Server-Side Apply (SSA) is a control plane subsystem that implements declarative resource management through field-level ownership tracking and intelligent merge semantics. Unlike client-side apply (which computes diffs locally), SSA shifts conflict resolution and ownership management to the API server, enabling robust multi-manager scenarios and reducing client-side complexity.\n\nThis guide explains how the subsystem is architected, how requests flow through the system, where conflicts are detected and resolved, and the operational tradeoffs involved.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nServer-Side Apply solves three core problems:\n\n1. **Ownership Tracking**: Who last modified which field? Without this, concurrent edits by different tools (kubectl, Helm, operators) cause data loss or unwanted overwrites.\n\n2. **Conflict Detection and Resolution**: When one manager tries to modify a field controlled by another, SSA detects the conflict and can either (a) fail with a clear error, (b) allow forced takeover, or (c) use structured merge semantics to prevent unintended overwrites.\n\n3. **Declarative State Management**: Clients declare *what they want* (via apply configurations) rather than *how to change it* (via imperative patches). The server reconciles the desired state with the live state and field ownership information.\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Included:**\n- Patch request handling for `application/apply-patch+yaml` and `application/apply-patch+cbor` content types (server-side apply patch types)\n- Declarative merge semantics using structured merge diff algorithms\n- Field ownership tracking via `metadata.managedFields`\n- Conflict detection and reporting when multiple managers compete for the same fields\n- Force-apply capability to override conflicts\n\n**Excluded:**\n- Client-side apply (using `kubectl apply` with `application/merge-patch+json`)\n- Strategic merge patch semantics (older merge-patch+json)\n- Imperative update/create operations (though these interact with SSA's field tracking)\n- Resource admission policies (though field managers validate against admission webhooks)\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\n1. **sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6**: The core merge and conflict detection algorithm. Used throughout field management to understand field boundaries and perform three-way merges.\n\n2. **k8s.io/kube-openapi**: Schema definitions (OpenAPI v3) describing which fields exist, their types, and merge strategies (e.g., merge list, replace list). Converted to internal type representations.\n\n3. **API server admission chain**: Mutating and validating admission controllers can modify objects and managedFields. Special validation ensures admission doesn't corrupt managedFields.\n\n4. **APIServer core request handling**: PatchResource handler in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` dispatches to SSA machinery.\n\n### Downstream Dependencies\n\n1. **kubectl**: Uses SSA via `kubectl apply` with `--server-side` flag, generating apply configurations from YAML manifests.\n\n2. **client-go libraries**: Generated apply configuration builders and helpers for programmatic SSA usage.\n\n3. **Controllers and operators**: Use SSA to safely manage resources in multi-tenant clusters.\n\n4. **etcd storage**: Stores the object and managedFields encoding. SSA doesn't manage storage directly but depends on storage being available.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Division\n\n### Component Hierarchy\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ PatchResource Handler                                       │\n│ (/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/                  │\n│  pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:PatchResource)            │\n└─────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────────┘\n                              │\n                ┌─────────────┼──────────────┬──────────────┐\n                │             │              │              │\n        ┌───────▼──────┐  ┌──▼──────┐  ┌───▼─────┐  ┌──────▼──────┐\n        │ jsonPatcher  │  │smpPatcher│  │applyPat-│  │fieldManager │\n        │              │  │          │  │cher     │  │Validating   │\n        │(JSON/Merge)  │  │(Strategic│  │(SSA)    │  │Admission    │\n        │              │  │ Merge)   │  │         │  │             │\n        └───────┬──────┘  └──┬───────┘  └────┬────┘  └──────┬──────┘\n                │            │               │              │\n                └────────────┼───────────────┼──────────────┘\n                             │\n          ┌──────────────────▼──────────────────┐\n          │  FieldManager (apimachinery)        │\n          │  (/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/   │\n          │   apimachinery/pkg/util/            │\n          │   managedfields/)                   │\n          └──────────────────┬──────────────────┘\n                             │\n          ┌──────────────────▼──────────────────┐\n          │ Structured Merge Diff (sigs.k8s.io) │\n          │ Three-way merge & conflict logic    │\n          └─────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Core Components\n\n#### 1. **PatchResource Handler** (`patch.go:PatchResource`)\n\n- **Entry point** for all PATCH requests to the API server\n- **Responsibility:**\n  - Parse incoming patch body and content-type header\n  - Create a `patcher` struct containing request state (name, namespace, patch bytes, field manager name, etc.)\n  - Select the appropriate patching mechanism based on content-type\n  - Call `patchResource()` which orchestrates the update flow\n  - Return the resulting object or error\n\n**Key decision:** Which patcher to use (jsonPatcher, smpPatcher, or applyPatcher) depends on content-type:\n  - `application/json-patch+json` → jsonPatcher (RFC6902 JSON Patch)\n  - `application/merge-patch+json` → jsonPatcher (RFC7386 JSON Merge Patch)\n  - `application/strategic-merge-patch+json` → smpPatcher (Kubernetes-specific merge)\n  - `application/apply-patch+yaml` or `+cbor` → applyPatcher (Server-Side Apply)\n\n#### 2. **Patcher Struct and Mechanisms** (`patch.go`)\n\nThe `patcher` struct holds all request context:\n\n```go\ntype patcher struct {\n    // Request metadata\n    name, namespace string\n    patchType types.PatchType\n    patchBytes []byte\n    userAgent string\n    options *metav1.PatchOptions // includes FieldManager name, Force, DryRun\n\n    // Validation and conversion\n    createValidation rest.ValidateObjectFunc\n    updateValidation rest.ValidateObjectUpdateFunc\n    admissionCheck admission.MutationInterface\n    codec runtime.Codec\n\n    // At-invocation-time fields\n    mechanism patchMechanism\n}\n```\n\n**Three concrete mechanisms implement `patchMechanism`:**\n\n1. **jsonPatcher** (`patch.go`)\n   - Applies JSON Patch or JSON Merge Patch\n   - Calls `fieldManager.UpdateNoErrors()` to track ownership via the FieldManager\n   - No force-conflict resolution; merges are straightforward patch application\n\n2. **smpPatcher** (`patch.go`)\n   - Applies strategic merge patch (SMP), the older Kubernetes merge strategy\n   - Understands merge directives in OpenAPI schema (e.g., patch strategy: merge vs. replace)\n   - Also calls `fieldManager.UpdateNoErrors()` for ownership tracking\n   - Used for backwards compatibility; not the primary SSA path\n\n3. **applyPatcher** (`patch.go`)\n   - **The SSA core mechanism**\n   - Marshals patch bytes as YAML/CBOR into an unstructured object\n   - Calls `fieldManager.Apply()` (not `UpdateNoErrors`)\n   - Supports `force` flag to override conflicts\n   - Validates with `FieldValidation` option (Warn/Strict/Ignore)\n\n#### 3. **FieldManager** (`apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/`)\n\nCentral to SSA. Tracks which manager owns which fields and performs three-way merges.\n\n**Public interface** (`managedfields.go`):\n```go\ntype FieldManager = internal.FieldManager\n\nfunc NewDefaultFieldManager(\n    typeConverter TypeConverter,\n    objectConverter runtime.ObjectConvertor,\n    objectDefaulter runtime.ObjectDefaulter,\n    objectCreater runtime.ObjectCreater,\n    kind schema.GroupVersionKind,\n    hub schema.GroupVersion,\n    subresource string,\n    resetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter,\n) (*FieldManager, error)\n```\n\n**Key methods**:\n- `Apply(liveObj, patchObj runtime.Object, fieldManager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, error)`: Performs three-way merge for SSA\n- `Update(liveObj, updateObj runtime.Object, manager string) (runtime.Object, error)`: Tracks fields modified by imperative updates\n- `UpdateNoErrors(liveObj, updateObj runtime.Object, manager string) runtime.Object`: Update without returning errors (used by JSON/SMP patchers)\n\n**Implementation** (`internal/fieldmanager.go`):\n- Wraps a Manager chain (see below) that handles different update types\n- Decodes managedFields from live object's metadata\n- Calls manager chain to compute new managedFields and merged object\n- Validates resulting managedFields before returning\n\n#### 4. **Manager Chain** (`internal/fieldmanager.go`)\n\nA sophisticated chain of responsibility pattern for handling different scenarios:\n\n```\nNewDefaultFieldManager(...)\n    ↓\nNewVersionCheckManager        // Checks API version compatibility\n    ↓\nNewLastAppliedUpdater        // Updates .metadata.annotations[\"kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration\"]\n    ↓\nNewLastAppliedManager        // Compatibility: handles old kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration\n    ↓\nNewProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager  // Optimization: only tracks ~1% of non-apply updates to reduce managedFields size\n    ↓\nNewCapManagersManager        // Caps number of managers (default 10); merges oldest entries if exceeded\n    ↓\nNewBuildManagerInfoManager   // Encodes manager name, operation timestamp, operation type into ManagedFieldsEntry\n    ↓\nNewManagedFieldsUpdater      // Updates managedFields in the object after merge\n    ↓\nNewStripMetaManager          // Strips metadata fields (uid, resourceVersion, etc.) from comparison\n    ↓\nStructuredMergeManager       // Core: performs actual three-way merge using sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff\n```\n\nEach layer adds orthogonal logic:\n- **StructuredMergeManager**: Does the actual three-way merge (`currentFields, ownedFields, desiredFields → mergedFields`)\n- **StripMetaManager**: Ignores system-managed metadata in merge\n- **ManagedFieldsUpdater**: Persists the manager info and field sets to object metadata\n- **BuildManagerInfoManager**: Encodes manager identity (name, subresource, operation type) into metadata\n- **CapManagersManager**: If >10 managers, merge oldest to keep managedFields bounded\n- **ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager**: Only 1% of non-apply updates are tracked (perf optimization)\n- **LastAppliedManager / LastAppliedUpdater**: Backwards compatibility with kubectl's old apply tracking\n\n#### 5. **Structured Merge Diff** (external: `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6`)\n\n- **Not in this repo**, but critical\n- Implements three-way merge algorithm\n- Understands field cardinality (scalar, map, list with merge strategy)\n- Detects conflicts when different managers claim ownership of same field\n- Returns `merge.Conflicts` if cannot resolve\n\n**Used by FieldManager to:**\n1. Decode live object into field sets (which fields exist, what values)\n2. Decode desired patch object into field sets (desired values, fields to set)\n3. Extract manager-owned field sets from managedFields\n4. Perform three-way merge: `Merge(live, desired, currentlyOwned) → merged + conflicts`\n\n#### 6. **Type Converter** (`apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/typeconverter.go`)\n\n- Converts OpenAPI schema definitions to internal type representations for structured-merge-diff\n- Maps K8s API types (Pod, Deployment, etc.) to field merge strategies from OpenAPI\n- Tells merge diff algorithm: \"This field is a map that merges by key X\" vs. \"This is a list that replaces wholesale\"\n\n**Used to answer:**\n- Is `spec.containers` a list that merges or replaces?\n- Are `spec.selector.matchLabels` map entries merged or replaced?\n\n#### 7. **Apply Configuration Builders** (`client-go/applyconfigurations/`)\n\n**Generated code** (by applyconfiguration-gen tool) that provides fluent APIs for building apply configurations.\n\nExample from `client-go/applyconfigurations/core/v1/pod.go`:\n\n```go\n// PodApplyConfiguration represents declarative configuration for Pod\ntype PodApplyConfiguration struct {\n    metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\",inline\"`\n    *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec *PodSpecApplyConfiguration `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status *PodStatusApplyConfiguration `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n\n// Pod constructs a PodApplyConfiguration\nfunc Pod(name, namespace string) *PodApplyConfiguration {\n    b := &PodApplyConfiguration{}\n    b.WithName(name)\n    b.WithNamespace(namespace)\n    b.WithKind(\"Pod\")\n    b.WithAPIVersion(\"v1\")\n    return b\n}\n\n// ExtractPodFrom extracts the applied configuration owned by a specific field manager\nfunc ExtractPodFrom(pod *corev1.Pod, fieldManager string, subresource string) (*PodApplyConfiguration, error) {\n    b := &PodApplyConfiguration{}\n    err := managedfields.ExtractInto(pod, internal.Parser().Type(\"io.k8s.api.core.v1.Pod\"), fieldManager, b, subresource)\n    if err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n    // ...\n    return b, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Three functions per resource type:**\n1. **Constructor** (`Pod(name, namespace)`): Creates a new ApplyConfiguration\n2. **Builder methods** (`WithSpec()`, `WithLabels()`): Fluent API to set fields\n3. **Extractor** (`ExtractPodFrom()`): Reads back the fields a manager owns from a live object\n\n#### 8. **Apply Configuration Generator** (`code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/`)\n\n- **Code generation tool** that creates the builders above from Go struct definitions\n- Reads Kubernetes API types (Pod, Deployment, etc.)\n- Generates pointer-to-pointer builders for nullable fields (idiomatic Go for optional fields)\n- Produces one file per type in the same package structure under `applyconfigurations/`\n\n#### 9. **Managed Fields Validating Admission Controller** (`fieldmanager/admission.go`)\n\n- Wraps the standard admission chain\n- After mutating admission runs, validates that managedFields is still valid JSON\n- If a buggy admission controller corrupts managedFields, this controller resets it to pre-admission state and warns\n- Prevents admission from creating invalid field ownership data\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow and Request Path\n\n### Scenario: User applies a deployment via `kubectl apply --server-side`\n\n#### Phase 1: Client Prepares the Request\n\n**Client-side (kubectl):**\n1. User runs: `kubectl apply --server-side -f deployment.yaml`\n2. kubectl parses `deployment.yaml` into a Kubernetes object\n3. kubectl generates an apply configuration using builders:\n   ```go\n   deploymentApplyConfig := applyconfigurations_v1.Deployment(\"my-deployment\", \"default\").\n       WithSpec(applyconfigurations_v1.DeploymentSpec().\n           WithReplicas(3).\n           WithSelector(...).\n           WithTemplate(...)).\n       WithLabels(...)\n   ```\n4. kubectl marshals the apply configuration to YAML (or CBOR if feature-gated)\n5. kubectl issues a PATCH request:\n   ```\n   PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/my-deployment\n   Content-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml\n   fieldManager: kubectl\n\n   [YAML bytes of apply configuration]\n   ```\n\n**Key:** The apply configuration is *incomplete*. It only includes fields the user cares about. System-generated fields (status, timestamps) are absent. This is critical: SSA interprets missing fields as \"I don't care about these.\"\n\n#### Phase 2: API Server Receives the Request\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:PatchResource()`**\n\n1. **Parse content-type and patch type:**\n   ```go\n   contentType := req.Header.Get(\"Content-Type\") // \"application/apply-patch+yaml\"\n   patchType := types.PatchType(contentType)     // types.ApplyYAMLPatchType\n   ```\n\n2. **Validate patch type is allowed:**\n   ```go\n   if !sets.NewString(patchTypes...).Has(contentType) {\n       scope.err(negotiation.NewUnsupportedMediaTypeError(patchTypes), w, req)\n       return\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Read and validate patch body:**\n   ```go\n   patchBytes, err := limitedReadBodyWithRecordMetric(ctx, req, scope.MaxRequestBodyBytes, ...)\n   ```\n\n4. **Parse PatchOptions from query params:**\n   ```go\n   options := &metav1.PatchOptions{}\n   metainternalversionscheme.ParameterCodec.DecodeParameters(req.URL.Query(), scope.MetaGroupVersion, options)\n   // Extracts: fieldManager, force, dryRun, fieldValidation\n   ```\n\n5. **Setup admission chain and validation:**\n   ```go\n   admit = fieldmanager.NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController(admit)\n   // Wraps admission to validate managedFields after mutating webhooks\n   ```\n\n6. **Create patcher struct:**\n   ```go\n   p := patcher{\n       namer: scope.Namer,\n       creater: scope.Creater,\n       defaulter: scope.Defaulter,\n       kind: scope.Kind,           // apps/v1/Deployment\n       resource: scope.Resource,   // deployments.apps.v1\n       patchType: types.ApplyYAMLPatchType,\n       patchBytes: patchBytes,\n       userAgent: req.UserAgent(),\n       options: options,           // includes fieldManager: \"kubectl\"\n       // ... (see patcher struct)\n   }\n   ```\n\n7. **Call patchResource:**\n   ```go\n   result, wasCreated, err := p.patchResource(ctx, scope)\n   ```\n\n#### Phase 3: Select and Initialize Patch Mechanism\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:patchResource()`**\n\n```go\nswitch p.patchType {\ncase types.ApplyYAMLPatchType:\n    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, yaml.Unmarshal, yaml.UnmarshalStrict)\n    p.forceAllowCreate = true  // SSA can create if object doesn't exist\n}\n```\n\n**ApplyPatcher initialized with:**\n- `fieldManager`: The *same* FieldManager that was initialized by the scope (contains TypeConverter, ObjectConverter, etc.)\n- Marshalers for YAML and strict YAML\n\n#### Phase 4: Apply Update Flow\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:patchResource()`**\n\nCreates a transformer chain:\n\n```go\ntransformers := []rest.TransformFunc{\n    p.applyPatch,               // Deserialization & patching\n    p.applyAdmission,           // Admission control\n    dedupOwnerReferencesTransformer,\n}\n\np.updatedObjectInfo = rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo(nil, transformers...)\n\n// Then calls the actual storage update\nresult, err := finisher.FinishRequest(ctx, func() (runtime.Object, error) {\n    options := patchToUpdateOptions(p.options)\n    updateObject, created, updateErr := p.restPatcher.Update(ctx, p.name, p.updatedObjectInfo,\n        p.createValidation, p.updateValidation, p.forceAllowCreate, options)\n    // p.restPatcher is the storage layer (typically etcd)\n    return updateObject, updateErr\n})\n```\n\nThis uses a retry loop with `GuaranteedUpdate` semantics: if the live object changes between read and write, retry with the latest live object.\n\n#### Phase 5: Patch Application\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:applyPatch()`**\n\nThis is called by the retry loop every iteration (potentially multiple times on conflict).\n\n```go\nfunc (p *patcher) applyPatch(ctx context.Context, _, currentObject runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\n    currentObjectHasUID, err := hasUID(currentObject)\n    if err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n\n    if !currentObjectHasUID {\n        // Object doesn't exist; create it\n        objToUpdate, patchErr := p.mechanism.createNewObject(ctx)\n    } else {\n        // Object exists; apply patch to it\n        objToUpdate, patchErr := p.mechanism.applyPatchToCurrentObject(ctx, currentObject)\n    }\n\n    // Validate UID consistency (if apply included a uid, ensure no uid mismatch)\n    // ...\n\n    return objToUpdate, nil\n}\n```\n\n#### Phase 6: Apply Patcher Executes SSA Merge\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject()`**\n\n```go\nfunc (p *applyPatcher) applyPatchToCurrentObject(requestContext context.Context, obj runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\n    force := false\n    if p.options.Force != nil {\n        force = *p.options.Force\n    }\n\n    // Deserialize the patch (YAML/CBOR) into an unstructured object\n    patchObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{Object: map[string]interface{}{}}\n    if err := p.unmarshalFn(p.patch, &patchObj.Object); err != nil {\n        return nil, errors.NewBadRequest(fmt.Sprintf(\"error decoding YAML: %v\", err))\n    }\n\n    // **THE CRITICAL CALL**: FieldManager.Apply() performs three-way merge\n    obj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n    if err != nil {\n        return obj, err  // Might be conflict error if force=false\n    }\n\n    // Validate field validation setting (Warn/Strict mode)\n    if p.validationDirective == metav1.FieldValidationStrict || metav1.FieldValidationWarn {\n        if err := p.unmarshalStrictFn(p.patch, &map[string]interface{}{}); err != nil {\n            if p.validationDirective == metav1.FieldValidationStrict {\n                return nil, errors.NewBadRequest(fmt.Sprintf(\"error strict decoding YAML: %v\", err))\n            }\n            addStrictDecodingWarnings(requestContext, []error{err})\n        }\n    }\n\n    return obj, nil\n}\n```\n\n#### Phase 7: FieldManager.Apply() — The Three-Way Merge\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:Apply()`**\n\n```go\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(liveObj, patchObj runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (runtime.Object, error) {\n    // Decode managedFields from live object\n    live, err := decodeLiveOrNew(liveObj, patchObj, false)\n    if err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n\n    // Call wrapped manager chain (handles versioning, last-applied, capping, etc.)\n    // The chain eventually calls StructuredMergeManager.Apply()\n    objToReturn, err := f.fieldManager.Apply(liveObj, patchObj, manager, force)\n    if err != nil {\n        return objToReturn, err\n    }\n\n    // Validate the resulting managedFields\n    if err := validateManagedFields(objToReturn); err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n\n    return objToReturn, nil\n}\n```\n\nThe manager chain processes this, eventually reaching `StructuredMergeManager.Apply()` (implemented by sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff):\n\n1. **Extract field sets:**\n   - `liveFieldSet`: Fields currently in the object\n   - `patchFieldSet`: Fields in the desired patch\n   - `ownedFieldSet`: Fields currently owned by this manager (from managedFields)\n\n2. **Three-way merge:**\n   ```\n   result := Merge(\n       currentObject: liveObj,\n       desiredObject: patchObj,\n       ownedFields: managedfields entry for this manager,\n       force: force flag\n   )\n   ```\n\n3. **Conflict detection:**\n   - If manager doesn't own a field but is trying to set it, and another manager owns it → conflict\n   - Example: User applies with fieldManager=\"kubectl\" trying to set `spec.replicas`, but fieldManager=\"operator\" already owns it → conflict\n\n4. **Force handling:**\n   - If `force=true` and conflict detected, take ownership of conflicting fields\n   - Merges old manager's field ownership with new manager's ownership\n\n5. **Update managedFields:**\n   - Create new ManagedFieldsEntry for this manager with the fields they now own\n   - Update timestamp, operation type, operation name\n\n#### Phase 8: Admission Control\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:applyAdmission()`**\n\n```go\nfunc (p *patcher) applyAdmission(ctx context.Context, patchedObject runtime.Object, currentObject runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\n    // Determine if this is a create or update\n    hasUID, err := hasUID(currentObject)\n    if !hasUID {\n        operation = admission.Create\n        currentObject = nil\n    } else {\n        operation = admission.Update\n    }\n\n    // Call admission controllers (mutating + validating)\n    if p.admissionCheck != nil && p.admissionCheck.Handles(operation) {\n        attributes := p.admissionAttributes(ctx, patchedObject, currentObject, operation, options)\n        return patchedObject, p.admissionCheck.Admit(ctx, attributes, p.objectInterfaces)\n    }\n\n    return patchedObject, nil\n}\n```\n\nAdmission controllers can:\n- Mutate the object (add labels, set defaults)\n- Reject with validation errors\n- Add warnings\n\nIf mutating admission modifies managedFields, the `NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController` wrapper validates and resets if corrupted.\n\n#### Phase 9: Storage Update with Retry\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`** (not shown in detail here)\n\nThe update goes to storage with a retry loop:\n\n1. Read latest live object from etcd\n2. Run all transformers (applyPatch, applyAdmission, etc.)\n3. If no conflict during write, success\n4. If conflict (ETag mismatch, another concurrent write), loop back to step 1 with new live object\n\n#### Phase 10: Response\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go:PatchResource()`**\n\n```go\nstatus := http.StatusOK\nif wasCreated {\n    status = http.StatusCreated\n}\n\ntransformResponseObject(ctx, scope, req, w, status, outputMediaType, result)\n```\n\n- If created: HTTP 201\n- If updated: HTTP 200\n- Response body: the resulting object (with managedFields populated)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Conflict Handling and Resolution Strategies\n\n### Conflict Anatomy\n\nA conflict occurs when:\n1. The current apply request (manager A) tries to modify field F\n2. Field F is currently owned by a different manager (manager B)\n3. Manager A does not have `force=true`\n\nExample:\n```yaml\n# Current object (after kubectl and operator both applied)\nmetadata:\n  managedFields:\n  - manager: kubectl\n    fields:\n      f:spec:\n        f:replicas: {}\n  - manager: operator\n    fields:\n      f:spec:\n        f:image: {}\n\n# User runs: kubectl apply --server-side\n# New patch sets: spec.replicas=5 (kubectl manager)\n# But operator manager owns spec.replicas → CONFLICT\n```\n\n### Conflict Detection\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go`**\n\n```go\nfunc NewConflictError(conflicts merge.Conflicts) *errors.StatusError {\n    causes := []metav1.StatusCause{}\n    for _, conflict := range conflicts {\n        causes = append(causes, metav1.StatusCause{\n            Type:    metav1.CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict,\n            Message: fmt.Sprintf(\"conflict with %v\", printManager(conflict.Manager)),\n            Field:   conflict.Path.String(),\n        })\n    }\n    return errors.NewApplyConflict(causes, getConflictMessage(conflicts))\n}\n```\n\nReturns HTTP 409 with details of conflicting fields and which manager owns each.\n\n### Resolution Strategies\n\n#### Strategy 1: Fail (Default)\n\n```\nRequest: apply with fieldManager=\"kubectl\" (no force)\nResponse: HTTP 409 Conflict\nError: \"Apply failed with 1 conflict: conflict with manager 'operator': spec.replicas\"\n```\n\nUser must either:\n- Manually remove the conflicting manager from object (rare)\n- Use `--force-conflicts` / `force=true` on the new apply request\n\n#### Strategy 2: Force Ownership Transfer\n\n```bash\nkubectl apply --server-side --force-conflicts\n```\n\nSets `force=true` in PatchOptions:\n\n```go\n// Overrides conflict: new manager takes ownership\nMerge(..., force=true) →\n    Removes old manager from managedFields for conflicting fields\n    Adds new manager to managedFields for those fields\n    Result: HTTP 200, object updated\n```\n\n**Risks of force:**\n- Silently removes another tool's field tracking\n- Can cause thrashing if two tools continuously force-apply conflicting changes\n- Should be used only when you're certain you're the intended owner\n\n#### Strategy 3: Three-Way Merge Prevention\n\nBest practice: **Design ownership boundaries.**\n\n- **kubectl** manages user-specified fields (image, replicas, labels)\n- **operator** manages system fields (status, internal configuration)\n\nUse different field sets to avoid conflicts:\n```yaml\n# kubectl manages these:\nmetadata:\n  labels:\n    app: myapp\nspec:\n  replicas: 3\n  template:\n    spec:\n      containers:\n      - name: app\n        image: myapp:1.0\n\n# operator manages these (via separate apply):\nstatus:\n  conditions: [...]\nspec:\n  internalConfig: {...}\n```\n\nBoth can apply without conflict because they never both claim the same field.\n\n#### Strategy 4: Re-Apply After Conflict\n\nSome workflows retry with `force=true`:\n\n```go\nfor attempt := 0; attempt < maxRetries; attempt++ {\n    resp, err := applyWithForce(false) // force=false\n    if err != nil && isConflict(err) && attempt < maxRetries-1 {\n        applyWithForce(true) // Try with force\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Conflict Prevention in Practice\n\n#### Test Case: `TestUpdateApplyConflict`\n\n**File: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager_test.go`**\n\n```go\nfunc TestUpdateApplyConflict(t *testing.T) {\n    f := managedfieldstest.NewTestFieldManager(\n        fakeTypeConverter,\n        schema.FromAPIVersionAndKind(\"apps/v1\", \"Deployment\"),\n    )\n\n    // First manager (e.g., kubectl) applies\n    patch1 := []byte(`{\n        \"metadata\": {\"labels\": {\"app\": \"nginx\"}},\n        \"spec\": {\n            \"replicas\": 3,\n            ...\n        }\n    }`)\n    obj1, err := f.Apply(emptyObj, patch1, \"manager1\", false)\n    // Success: manager1 owns spec.replicas\n\n    // Second manager tries to apply same field\n    patch2 := []byte(`{\n        \"spec\": {\"replicas\": 5}\n    }`)\n    obj2, err := f.Apply(obj1, patch2, \"manager2\", false)\n    // Error: Conflict! manager1 owns spec.replicas\n\n    // Now with force\n    obj3, err := f.Apply(obj1, patch2, \"manager2\", true)\n    // Success: manager2 takes over ownership\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Failure Mode 1: Corrupted managedFields\n\n**Cause:** Buggy mutating admission webhook modifies managedFields incorrectly\n\n**Detection:**\n```go\nif err := managedfields.ValidateManagedFields(encodedManagedFields); err != nil {\n    // Admission corrupted managedFields\n}\n```\n\n**Recovery:**\n```go\n// NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController\nif err := managedfields.ValidateManagedFields(managedFieldsAfterAdmission); err != nil {\n    objectMeta.SetManagedFields(managedFieldsBeforeAdmission)  // Reset\n    warning.AddWarning(ctx, \"\", \"managedFields was in an invalid state after admission\")\n}\n```\n\n**User Impact:** Fields marked corrupted are reset; user sees warning but apply succeeds.\n\n### Failure Mode 2: Uncontrolled managedFields Growth\n\n**Cause:** Too many different field managers (e.g., flapping between tools)\n\n**Example:** 100 different CI systems apply the same resource with different manager names\n\n**Limit:** `DefaultMaxUpdateManagers = 10`\n\n**Recovery:**\n```go\n// CapManagersManager merges oldest entries\nif len(managers) > 10 {\n    // Merge manager #1 into manager #2\n    // Consolidates ownership records\n}\n```\n\n**Consequence:** Very old manager records are lost; field ownership history truncated\n\n**Design tradeoff:**\n- Could make this configurable, but default 10 is conservative\n- Prevents unbounded etcd growth but loses granular historical tracking\n- Acceptable: most clusters have ~3-5 managers per resource\n\n### Failure Mode 3: Patch Too Large (Objects)\n\n**Cause:** Apply configuration + live object + managedFields exceeds storage limit\n\n**Limit:** Typically ~1 MB per object (etcd limit)\n\n**Recovery:**\n```go\nif isTooLargeError(err) && p.patchType != types.ApplyYAMLPatchType && ... {\n    // Clear managedFields and retry\n    // (Not done for SSA to preserve field tracking)\n    p.updatedObjectInfo = rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo(nil,\n        p.applyPatch,\n        p.applyAdmission,\n        func(...) (runtime.Object, error) {\n            accessor, _ := meta.Accessor(obj)\n            accessor.SetManagedFields(nil)  // Clear managedFields, try again\n            return obj, nil\n        })\n    result, err = requestFunc()\n}\n```\n\n**User Impact:** Auto-retry after clearing managedFields (non-SSA only). For SSA, the request fails.\n\n**Design tradeoff:**\n- SSA explicitly does NOT clear managedFields because field tracking is critical to correctness\n- Client must reduce object complexity or split into multiple objects\n\n### Failure Mode 4: Resource Version Conflicts (Optimistic Locking)\n\n**Cause:** Two concurrent requests modify the same resource\n\n**Example:**\n1. Request A reads object (resourceVersion=100)\n2. Request B reads object (resourceVersion=100)\n3. Request B writes (resourceVersion=101)\n4. Request A tries to write with resourceVersion=100 → CONFLICT\n\n**Recovery:**\n```go\n// In storage layer: GuaranteedUpdate loop\nfor {\n    obj := storage.Get(key)  // Get latest\n    transformedObj := transform(obj)\n    if !storage.Update(key, transformedObj, obj.resourceVersion) {\n        continue  // Retry with latest\n    }\n    break\n}\n```\n\n**User Impact:** Transparent retry. Apply succeeds after a few milliseconds (unless load is extreme).\n\n### Failure Mode 5: Type Converter Cache Stale\n\n**Cause:** OpenAPI schema changes after FieldManager is initialized\n\n**Cause:** Upgrade cluster, update CRD schema\n\n**Impact:** Three-way merge uses outdated field merge strategies\n\n**Prevention:**\n- FieldManager is initialized per API server process\n- Schema changes require API server restart to pick up\n- CRD changes are watched, but integration is complex\n\n### Design Tradeoff 1: Ownership Model\n\n**Choice:** Field-level ownership via managedFields\n\n**Alternatives:**\n- Resource-level: Track which manager last touched the object (simpler, less precise)\n- Operation-level: Track every operation's conflicts (more history, unbounded storage)\n\n**Why fields?**\n- Allows multiple managers to control different fields of same object\n- Kubectl (labels, spec) + operator (status) on same Pod without conflict\n- Matches mental model: \"I own this part of the spec\"\n\n**Cost:**\n- Larger managedFields entries\n- More complex merge algorithm\n- Harder to explain to users (\"why do I have a conflict?\")\n\n### Design Tradeoff 2: Three-Way Merge vs. Two-Way\n\n**Choice:** Three-way: compare desired + current + previously-owned\n\n**Alternatives:**\n- Two-way: just compare desired + current (traditional JSON merge patch behavior)\n- Client-driven: client computes diff and sends operations (JSON Patch)\n\n**Why three-way?**\n- Prevents data loss: can detect \"did someone else modify this field?\"\n- Enables force: can precisely know what to take over\n- Supports multiple managers: can track ownership lineage\n\n**Cost:**\n- Harder to debug (\"why did my change not apply?\")\n- Requires accurate managedFields (garbage in = garbage out)\n\n### Design Tradeoff 3: Apply Semantics for Lists\n\n**Choice:** Merge lists by default (can be overridden per-field in OpenAPI)\n\n**Example:**\n```yaml\nspec:\n  containers:\n  - name: app\n    image: myapp:1.0\n```\n\nIf you apply again with:\n```yaml\nspec:\n  containers:\n  - name: app\n    image: myapp:2.0\n  - name: sidecar\n    image: sidecar:1.0\n```\n\nResult: Both containers (merged), not just the sidecar.\n\n**Alternatives:**\n- Replace: Applying this would remove the original container\n- Add: Applying would append always (no updates)\n\n**Why merge?**\n- Intuitive: \"I want containers A and B\" means \"ensure I have A and B\"\n- Matches declarative paradigm: state what you want, server reconciles\n\n**Cost:**\n- List order can matter for some workloads\n- Users sometimes expect replace semantics\n- Requires OpenAPI hint to override (e.g., `x-kubernetes-patch-strategy: replace`)\n\n### Operational Limits\n\n| Limit | Value | Impact |\n|-------|-------|--------|\n| Max field managers per object | 10 | After 10, oldest entries merged |\n| Max managedFields entry size | ~10 KB | Very large field sets need chunking |\n| Max patch size | Usually 1-10 MB | Limited by API server's max request body |\n| Patch request timeout | Usually 30-60s | Long-running merges on huge objects |\n| Max retries (conflicts) | Unlimited in FieldManager | HTTP handler may timeout first |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### Extension Point 1: Custom TypeConverter\n\n**Purpose:** Teach field manager about your custom types\n\n**Location:** Initialization of FieldManager in APIServer boot\n\n**File:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/request_scope.go` (not shown, but creates scope.FieldManager)\n\n**How:**\n```go\ntypeConverter := managedfields.NewTypeConverter(\n    openAPIDefinitions,  // From OpenAPI schema\n    disallowUnknownFields, // Strict mode\n)\n\nfieldManager, err := managedfields.NewDefaultFieldManager(\n    typeConverter,\n    unsafeConvertor,\n    defaulter,\n    creater,\n    gvk,\n    hubVersion,\n    subresource,\n    resetFields,  // Reset fields on create\n)\n```\n\n**Customization Example:**\n- If you have a custom type that needs special merge logic, define it in OpenAPI\n- Add `x-kubernetes-patch-merge-key` and `x-kubernetes-patch-strategy` annotations\n- TypeConverter reads these and configures merge diff behavior\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect merge strategy can cause data loss or unexpected merges.\n\n### Extension Point 2: Admission Webhooks + Field Tracking\n\n**Purpose:** Mutating webhooks can modify objects; we must track their changes in managedFields\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`\n\n**How:**\n```go\nadmit = fieldmanager.NewManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController(admit)\n```\n\n**What happens:**\n1. Before admission: snapshot managedFields\n2. Call admission webhooks\n3. After admission: validate managedFields (structured-merge-diff's internal format)\n4. If corrupted, reset to snapshot and warn\n\n**Hook:** Mutating webhooks are called through the normal admission chain.\n\n**Customization:** Write a webhook that transforms objects:\n```go\n// Your webhook receives the Pod\n// You can set status.conditions, inject sidecar containers, etc.\n// The FieldManager will:\n// - Track fields set by this webhook in the \"system\" manager\n// - Report conflicts if another manager owns these fields\n```\n\n**Risk:**\n- Webhook adds a field that another manager owns → conflict\n- Webhook is too slow → SSA request times out\n- Webhook crashes → request fails\n\n### Extension Point 3: Reset Fields Specification\n\n**Purpose:** Configure which fields are \"system-managed\" and should not be owned by field managers\n\n**Location:** FieldManager initialization\n\n**File:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/request_scope.go` (not visible)\n\n**Example:**\n```go\nresetFields := map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter{\n    fieldpath.APIVersion(\"v1\"): fieldpath.Filter{\n        \"metadata\": {\"managedFields\", \"resourceVersion\", \"uid\"},\n    },\n}\n\nfieldManager, _ := managedfields.NewDefaultFieldManager(..., resetFields)\n```\n\n**Effect:** Fields in resetFields are never included in managedFields. They're managed by the system.\n\n**Customization:** Define which fields of your CRD are system-managed:\n```go\n// In your API type's openapi definition\nresetFields[myGVK] = fieldpath.Filter{\n    \"status\": fieldpath.Filter{},  // Entire status is system-managed\n    \"metadata\": {...},\n}\n```\n\n### Extension Point 4: Custom FieldManager Name\n\n**Purpose:** Disambiguate who made the change\n\n**How:** Users pass `fieldManager` query parameter or header:\n```bash\nkubectl apply --server-side --field-manager=my-controller-v1.0\n```\n\n**Location:** PatchOptions parsing in patch.go\n```go\noptions := &metav1.PatchOptions{}\n// fieldManager extracted from options.FieldManager field\n```\n\n**Customization:** SDKs and controllers choose unique names:\n```go\n// client-go apply request builder\nreq, err := apply.NewRequest(client, podApplyConfig)\n// Uses feature-gated default fieldManager name\n```\n\n**Risk:** If multiple processes use the same fieldManager name, they're treated as one entity (conflicts are harder to track).\n\n### Extension Point 5: OpenAPI Schema Customization\n\n**Purpose:** Define merge strategies for your types\n\n**Location:** OpenAPI v3 annotations on struct fields\n\n**Example:** In a CRD or API type:\n\n```go\n// In k8s.io/api/core/v1/pod.go\ntype PodSpec struct {\n    // +kubebuilder:validation:MinItems=1\n    // +listType=set\n    // +listMapKey=name\n    Containers []Container `json:\"containers\" protobuf:\"bytes,2,rep,name=containers\"`\n}\n```\n\nAnnotations translate to OpenAPI:\n```yaml\nspec.containers:\n  type: array\n  items:\n    $ref: \"#/components/schemas/Container\"\n  x-kubernetes-list-type: set\n  x-kubernetes-list-map-keys: [name]\n  x-kubernetes-patch-strategy: merge\n  x-kubernetes-patch-merge-key: name\n```\n\n**Customization:** In your CRD:\n```yaml\nproperties:\n  spec:\n    type: object\n    properties:\n      workers:\n        type: array\n        x-kubernetes-list-type: map\n        x-kubernetes-list-map-keys: [name]\n        items:\n          type: object\n```\n\n**Risk:** Wrong merge strategy causes unintended overwrites. E.g., if you say \"replace\" but mean \"merge\", applying twice removes entries.\n\n### Extension Point 6: Dry-Run and Field Validation\n\n**Purpose:** Safely preview changes and detect schema issues before committing\n\n**How:**\n```bash\nkubectl apply --server-side --dry-run=server\nkubectl apply --server-side --field-validation=strict\n```\n\n**Parameters:** Query params on PATCH request:\n```\n?dryRun=All&fieldValidation=Strict\n```\n\n**Location:** PatchOptions parsing and handling\n- `dryRun`: Specifies if request should actually modify storage\n- `fieldValidation`: Warn, Strict, or Ignore unknown fields\n\n**Customization:** In client code:\n```go\noptions := &metav1.PatchOptions{\n    DryRun: []string{metav1.DryRunAll},\n    FieldValidation: metav1.FieldValidationStrict,\n}\nreq := client.Patch(ctx, pod, types.ApplyPatchType).\n    SubResource(something).\n    VersionedParams(options, ...)\n```\n\n**Safety:**\n- Dry-run: Request is processed fully but not persisted to etcd\n- fieldValidation: Strict rejects unknown fields; Warn allows but returns warnings\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directories Map\n\n### Core Request Handling\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | Main patch `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/kubectl/pkg/cmd/apply/apply_test.go` | Test suite for kubectl apply command |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Operational Implications and Best Practices\n\n### Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Merge Complexity\n\n**Worst case:** O(n) where n = number of fields in object\n\n- OpenAPI schema lookup: O(1) hash\n- Three-way merge: Walk live object fields once\n- managedFields encoding/decoding: Fixed overhead per entry\n\n**Typical:** 1-5 ms for a 1 KB Pod, 10-50 ms for a 100 KB Deployment\n\n**Bottleneck:** Large objects with many fields\n- Each field lookup traverses the schema\n- Large lists cause array comparisons\n- managedFields with 10 manager entries increases overhead\n\n#### managedFields Storage Cost\n\n**Per-object overhead:** 1-10 KB\n\nExample: Small Pod with 3 managers:\n```yaml\nmetadata:\n  managedFields:\n  - manager: kubectl\n    time: 2024-01-01T00:00:00Z\n    fieldsV1:\n      f:metadata:\n        f:labels:\n          f:app: {}\n      f:spec:\n        f:containers: {}\n  # ... (2 more manager entries)\n```\n\n**Storage impact:**\n- etcd size ~5-10% larger due to managedFields\n- Every update rewrites managedFields → extra write amplification\n- Solution: Monitor object sizes; split large objects if needed\n\n#### Request Latency Under Conflict\n\n**No conflict:** 5-10 ms\n\n**With conflict:** 50-200 ms (after retry loop)\n\n- Conflict detected → HTTP 409\n- Client (or kubectl) retries with `force=true`\n- Second apply succeeds\n\n**Risk:** Conflict storms if two tools continuously force-apply:\n```\nTime 0: Tool A applies (success)\nTime 5ms: Tool B applies (conflict, retries with force)\nTime 10ms: Tool A applies (conflict, retries with force)\nTime 15ms: Tool B applies (conflict, retries with force)\n... (thrashing)\n```\n\n**Mitigation:** Design non-overlapping field ownership; use separate managers for different concerns.\n\n### Reliability Patterns\n\n#### Pattern 1: Idempotent Applies\n\nSSA is idempotent: applying the same config twice produces the same result (no spurious field ownership changes).\n\n**Example:**\n```bash\nkubectl apply --server-side -f pod.yaml  # Apply 1\nkubectl apply --server-side -f pod.yaml  # Apply 2 (same result)\n```\n\n**Benefit:** Safe to retry on transient failures (network, timeouts)\n\n**Exception:** If another manager modifies fields between applies, conflict may occur\n\n#### Pattern 2: Multi-Manager Ownership\n\n**Design principle:** Partition field ownership by concern.\n\n```yaml\n# App: manages spec.containers, spec.volumes\napiVersion: v1\nkind: Pod\nmetadata:\n  name: app\n  namespace: default\nspec:\n  containers:\n  - name: app\n    image: app:1.0\n  volumes:\n  - name: data\n    emptyDir: {}\n\n# Operator: manages status.conditions, metadata.annotations\nmetadata:\n  annotations:\n    operator-managed: \"true\"\nstatus:\n  conditions:\n  - type: Ready\n    status: \"True\"\n```\n\n**Result:** Each manager owns disjoint fields; no conflicts.\n\n#### Pattern 3: Conflict Detection as Operational Signal\n\nWhen a conflict occurs, it's often a sign of misconfiguration:\n\n```\nkubectl apply error: \"Apply failed with 1 conflict: conflict with manager 'operator': spec.replicas\"\n```\n\n**Response:**\n1. Identify which manager owns the field (operator in this case)\n2. Determine root cause: Is operator supposed to manage replicas? Or should kubectl?\n3. Update ownership design or remove conflicting manager\n\n**Anti-pattern:** Reflexively using `--force-conflicts` to bypass conflicts. This suggests design issues.\n\n### Reliability Under Failures\n\n#### Scenario 1: Admission Webhook Crashes\n\n**What happens:**\n1. Apply reaches admission stage\n2. Webhook crashes or times out\n3. Request fails; object not modified\n\n**Recovery:** Webhook operator fixes issue; user retries apply\n\n**Guarantee:** managedFields remains consistent (untouched if admission fails)\n\n#### Scenario 2: API Server Crashes During Apply\n\n**What happens:**\n1. Apply request received, partially processed\n2. API server process dies\n3. Storage layer has partially-written object or no write at all\n\n**Recovery:**\n- If write committed: etcd has new object; crash is transparent\n- If write not committed: No change; next retry will work\n\n**Guarantee:** No orphaned or corrupted managedFields (etcd transactions ensure atomicity)\n\n#### Scenario 3: Network Partition During Apply\n\n**What happens:**\n1. Client sends apply request\n2. Request reaches API server, fully processed\n3. Client disconnects before seeing response\n\n**Result:** Object IS modified; client thinks it failed\n\n**Recovery:** Client retries; second apply is idempotent (same fields owned, no conflict)\n\n**No**: managedFields is not double-tracked\n\n### Monitoring and Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics to Monitor\n\n1. **Apply Request Latency:** Histogram of PATCH request latencies for SSA\n   - Normal: 5-20 ms\n   - Alert if: > 100 ms (sign of schema lookup slowness, conflicts, or retry loops)\n\n2. **Conflict Rate:** Count of HTTP 409 responses from apply requests\n   - Normal: < 1% of applies\n   - Alert if: > 5% (sign of ownership design issues or tool thrashing)\n\n3. **managedFields Entry Count:** Per resource type\n   - Normal: 2-5 managers\n   - Alert if: Consistently > 10 (capped; oldest being dropped)\n\n4. **Object Size by Type:** Monitor etcd size growth\n   - If managedFields overhead > 20% of object, consider redesign\n\n#### Logging\n\nAPI server logs:\n```\nlevel=info verb=PATCH user=admin@example.com result=success latency=15ms object=Pod/default/my-pod\nlevel=warn verb=PATCH user=tool@example.com result=conflict latency=50ms object=Pod/default/my-pod reason=\"conflict with manager 'operator'\"\n```\n\nAlerts on conflict patterns:\n- Same object conflicted > 5 times in 1 minute\n- Different objects conflicted within milliseconds (sign of tool thrashing)\n\n### Common Pitfalls\n\n#### Pitfall 1: Assuming Patch Deletes Omitted Fields\n\n**Misconception:** \"If I apply with only `spec.replicas=3`, it will delete other spec fields\"\n\n**Reality:** Omitted fields are left untouched. Apply sets what you specify; doesn't delete the rest.\n\n**Example:**\n```yaml\n# Current object\nspec:\n  replicas: 5\n  template:\n    spec:\n      containers:\n      - name: app\n        image: app:1.0\n\n# Apply:\nspec:\n  replicas: 3\n# (no template specified)\n\n# Result:\nspec:\n  replicas: 3  # Changed\n  template:    # UNCHANGED (still has containers)\n    spec:\n      containers:\n      - name: app\n        image: app:1.0\n```\n\n**Solution:** Use kubectl to compute what's omitted; don't rely on \"implicit delete\"\n\n#### Pitfall 2: Mixing Apply and Imperative Updates\n\n**Scenario:**\n```bash\nkubectl apply --server-side -f pod.yaml  # SSA tracks ownership\nkubectl set image deployment/app app=app:2.0  # Imperative update\nkubectl apply --server-side -f pod.yaml  # Conflict!\n```\n\n**Why conflict:** Imperative `set image` doesn't know about SSA ownership; it just updates the object. When you apply again, SSA sees the image was changed by someone else.\n\n**Solution:** Stick to one method (apply) for a resource; don't mix with imperative updates\n\n#### Pitfall 3: Assuming Force Means \"Safe\"\n\n**Misconception:** \"Using `--force-conflicts` is always safe\"\n\n**Reality:** Force blindly takes ownership, removing another manager's claim. If used repeatedly, can destabilize multi-manager coordination.\n\n**Example:**\n```bash\nTool A: kubectl apply --force-conflicts  # Takes ownership of spec.replicas\nTool B: kubectl apply --force-conflicts  # Takes ownership of spec.replicas\nTool A: kubectl apply --force-conflicts  # Takes ownership back\n...\n# Thrashing; neither tool's intent is stable\n```\n\n**Solution:** Use force only to recover from misconfiguration; then redesign ownership.\n\n#### Pitfall 4: Custom Types Without OpenAPI\n\n**Scenario:** You define a CRD but don't provide OpenAPI schema\n\n**Result:** FieldManager defaults to treating lists as \"replace\" (not merge)\n\n**Example:**\n```yaml\n# CRD without proper x-kubernetes-list-type annotation\nspec:\n  workers:\n  - name: w1\n    role: primary\n  - name: w2\n    role: secondary\n\n# Apply 1: Creates both workers\n# Apply 2: Specifies only w1 → w2 DELETED (because list is \"replace\")\n```\n\n**Solution:** Always provide OpenAPI schema with proper annotations; use `x-kubernetes-list-type: map` and `x-kubernetes-list-map-keys` for lists.\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nKubernetes Server-Side Apply is a sophisticated subsystem that shifts conflict resolution and ownership tracking from clients to the API server. Its power lies in enabling safe, multi-manager coordination through field-level ownership and three-way merge semantics.\n\n**Key takeaways:**\n\n1. **Ownership matters**: managedFields is the single source of truth for who controls what\n2. **Conflicts are signals**: They indicate misconfiguration; resolve by redesigning ownership boundaries\n3. **Apply is idempotent**: Can safely retry; no risk of double-applying\n4. **Design for non-overlaps**: Partition fields by manager to avoid conflicts\n5. **Use force sparingly**: It's a sledgehammer; use only to recover from misconfiguration\n\nFor operators and controllers, SSA provides a safer alternative to imperative object modification, reducing the risk of data loss in multi-tenant, multi-tool scenarios.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1990,"cache_read_input_tokens":61036,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1990},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"97e44fa8-9ff8-4b09-a9a5-7794dfbd2cdb","uuid":"54982ca2-fc18-452c-8c78-7ee19c93b657"}
